<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">1934 FIFA World Cup</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p>The <b>1934 FIFA World Cup</b> was the second <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a>, the world championship for <a href="/wiki/List_of_men%27s_national_association_football_teams" title="List of men's national association football teams">men's national</a> <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> teams. It took place in Italy from 27 May to 10 June 1934.</p>
<p>The 1934 World Cup was the first for which teams had to <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="FIFA World Cup qualification">qualify</a> to take part. Thirty-two nations entered the competition, and after qualification, 16 teams participated in the finals tournament. Reigning champions <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_national_football_team" title="Uruguay national football team">Uruguay</a> did not enter. <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> became the second World Cup champions, beating <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia_national_football_team" title="Czechoslovakia national football team">Czechoslovakia</a> 2–1 in the final.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Host_selection">Host selection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1934_FIFA_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Host selection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_hosts" title="FIFA World Cup hosts">FIFA World Cup hosts</a></div>
<p>After a lengthy decision-making process in which FIFA's executive committee met eight times,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Italy was chosen as the host nation at a meeting in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a> on 9 October 1932.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-h23_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-h23-3">[3]</a></sup> The decision was taken by the executive committee without a ballot of members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-h23_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-h23-3">[3]</a></sup> The Italian bid was chosen in preference to one from Sweden;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIFAhistory_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-FIFAhistory-4">[4]</a></sup> the Italian government assigned a budget of 3.5 million <a href="/wiki/Italian_lira" title="Italian lira">lire</a> to the tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Qualification_and_participants">Qualification and participants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1934_FIFA_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Qualification and participants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1934_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="1934 FIFA World Cup qualification">1934 FIFA World Cup qualification</a></div>
<p>36 countries applied to enter the tournament, so qualifying matches were required to thin the field to 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-h23_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-h23-3">[3]</a></sup> Even so, there were several notable absentees. Reigning World Cup holders <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_national_football_team" title="Uruguay national football team">Uruguay</a> declined to participate, in protest at the refusal of several European countries to travel to South America for the <a href="/wiki/1930_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1930 FIFA World Cup">previous World Cup</a>, which Uruguay had hosted in 1930.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> As a result, the 1934 World Cup is the only one in which the reigning champions did not participate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The British <a href="/wiki/Home_Nations" title="Home Nations">Home Nations</a>, in a period of self-imposed exile from FIFA, also refused to participate. <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">Football Association</a> committee member <a href="/wiki/Charles_Sutcliffe" title="Charles Sutcliffe">Charles Sutcliffe</a>'s view was: "the national associations of England, Scotland, Wales and Ireland have quite enough to do in their <a href="/wiki/British_Home_Championship" title="British Home Championship">own International Championship</a> which seems to me a far better World Championship than the one to be staged in Rome".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite their role as hosts, <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> were still required to qualify, the first and only time the host nation was not granted automatic qualification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-h23_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-h23-3">[3]</a></sup> The qualifying matches were arranged on a geographical basis. Withdrawals by <a href="/wiki/Chile_national_football_team" title="Chile national football team">Chile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peru_national_football_team" title="Peru national football team">Peru</a> meant <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazil</a> qualified without playing a single match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Twelve of the 16 places were allocated to Europe, three to the Americas, and one to Africa or Asia (including Turkey). Only 10 of the 32 entrants, and four of the 16 qualified teams (Brazil, Argentina, United States and Egypt, the first African team to qualify for a World Cup finals tournament), were from outside Europe. The last place in the finals was contested between the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a> only three days before the start of the tournament in a one-off match in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, which the United States won.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>The majority of the 16 teams were making their first World Cup appearance. These included nine of the 12 European teams (Italy, Germany, Spain, the Netherlands, Hungary, Czechoslovakia, Sweden, Austria, and Switzerland) together with Egypt. Egypt were the first team from Africa in the finals and would not qualify again until the next time the competition was held in Italy, in 1990.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy_as_hosts">Italy as hosts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1934_FIFA_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Italy as hosts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Like the <a href="/wiki/1936_Summer_Olympics" title="1936 Summer Olympics">Berlin Olympics</a> two years later, the 1934 World Cup was a high-profile instance of a sporting event being used for overt political gain. <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a> was keen to use the tournament as a means of promoting fascism.</p>
<div class="noviewer thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px">

<p>The number of supporters travelling from other countries was higher than at any previous football tournament, including 7,000 from the Netherlands and 10,000 each from Austria and Switzerland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Format">Format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1934_FIFA_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The group stage used in the first World Cup was discarded in favour of a straight knockout tournament. If a match was tied after ninety minutes, then thirty minutes of extra time were played. If the score was still tied after extra time, the match would be replayed the next day.</p>
<p>The eight seeded teams – Argentina, Brazil, Germany, Italy, the Netherlands, Austria, Czechoslovakia and Hungary – were kept apart in the first round.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Summary">Summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1934_FIFA_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For a list of all squads that appeared in the final tournament, see <a href="/wiki/1934_FIFA_World_Cup_squads" title="1934 FIFA World Cup squads">1934 FIFA World Cup squads</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1934_FIFA_World_Cup.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/1934_FIFA_World_Cup.png/400px-1934_FIFA_World_Cup.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/1934_FIFA_World_Cup.png/600px-1934_FIFA_World_Cup.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/1934_FIFA_World_Cup.png/800px-1934_FIFA_World_Cup.png 2x" width="400"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1934_FIFA_World_Cup.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Qualifying countries and their results</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>All eight first round matches kicked off at the same time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Hosts and favourites Italy won handsomely, defeating the USA 7–1; <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> correspondent wrote that "only the fine goal-tending of <a href="/wiki/Julius_Hjulian" title="Julius Hjulian">Julius Hjulian</a> of Chicago kept the score as low as it was".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Internal disputes meant Argentina's squad for the tournament did not contain a single member of the team which had reached the final in 1930.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Against Sweden in Bologna, Argentina twice took the lead, but two goals by <a href="/wiki/Sven_Jonasson" title="Sven Jonasson">Sven Jonasson</a> and a winner by <a href="/wiki/Knut_Kroon" title="Knut Kroon">Knut Kroon</a> gave Sweden a 3–2 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Fellow South Americans Brazil also suffered an early exit. Spain beat them comfortably; 3–1 the final score.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>For the only time in World Cup history, the last eight consisted entirely of European teams – <a href="/wiki/Austria_national_football_team" title="Austria national football team">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia_national_football_team" title="Czechoslovakia national football team">Czechoslovakia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary_national_football_team" title="Hungary national football team">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">Sweden</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a>. All four non-European teams who made the journey to Italy were eliminated after one match.</p>
<p>In the quarter-finals, the first replayed match in World Cup history took place, when Italy and Spain drew 1–1 after extra time. The match was played in a highly aggressive manner with several players of both sides injured: rough play injured the Spanish goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Zamora" title="Ricardo Zamora">Ricardo Zamora</a> in the first match, leaving him unable to participate in the replay, while on the other side even rougher play by Spaniards broke the leg of the Italian <a href="/wiki/Mario_Pizziolo" title="Mario Pizziolo">Mario Pizziolo</a> who would not play in the national team again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Italy won the replay 1–0, their play so physical that at least three Spaniards had to depart the field with injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Italy then went on to beat Austria in the semi-finals by the same score. Meanwhile, Czechoslovakia secured their place in the final by beating Germany 3–1.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Stadio_Nazionale_PNF" title="Stadio Nazionale PNF">Stadium of the National Fascist Party</a> was the venue for the final. With 80 minutes played, the Czechoslovaks led 1–0. The Italians managed to score before the final whistle, and then added another goal in extra time to be crowned World Cup winners.</p>
<p>Italy's total of three goals conceded in five matches was a record low for a team winning the World Cup. It was matched by England in <a href="/wiki/1966_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1966 FIFA World Cup">1966</a> (who played six matches) and Brazil in <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994</a> (who played seven), but was not surpassed until <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998</a> when France won the World Cup conceding only two goals over seven games, a record later matched by Italy in <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006</a> and Spain in <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Squads">Squads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1934_FIFA_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Squads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>For a list of all squads that appeared in the final tournament, see <i><a href="/wiki/1934_FIFA_World_Cup_squads" title="1934 FIFA World Cup squads">1934 FIFA World Cup squads</a></i>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_round">First round</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1934_FIFA_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: First round">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Goalscorers">Goalscorers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1934_FIFA_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Goalscorers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>With five goals, Oldřich Nejedlý is the top scorer in the tournament. In total, 70 goals were scored by 45 different players, with none of them credited as own goal.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="FIFA_retrospective_ranking">FIFA retrospective ranking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1934_FIFA_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: FIFA retrospective ranking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 1986, FIFA published a report that ranked all teams in each World Cup up to and including 1986, based on progress in the competition, overall results and quality of the opposition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The rankings for the 1934 tournament were as follows:</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Federale_102">Federale 102</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1934_FIFA_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Federale 102">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Federale 102, which was manufactured in Italy, was the match ball provided for the 1934 World Cup.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
